its really interesting to me that og ena and dbbq ena have distinct personalities outside of their different "sides" (sad, meanie, salesmen, happy), that is, the way that these 'sides' interact with each other. og ena's sides are an simply exaggeration of her emotional state, ena is by nature a sweet and sensitive person, and both sides represent these aspects of her personality, despite acting so differently. they dont feel like different people until she turns her sad side into a mask that looks and acts like a separate parasitic entity. this is a good metaphor for how masking your true emotions causes a disconnect in identity, because your emotions are part of who you are. meanwhile dbbq ena's sides interact quite differently. her salesperson side is optimistic and cheerful like og ena's happy side, but way less genuine. kinda like how a worker in retail acts friendly and cheery towards customers, not because they actually feel that way, but because they'll get fired if they don't. salesperson is not an emotion, but a mask.  dbbq ena's meanie side on the other hand more than just "angry", she's tired, brash, sarcastic, self-loathing, and desperate to complete her job so she can finally be free. whenever ena expresses genuine emotion and desires, she only uses her meanie side because it represents who she truly is as a person.

I took ADHD medication for the first time today  I think i finally understand this episode  Maybe it wasnt intended to be understood in this way but ive watched this episode like 20 times since it came out and never got it  But now i think i do  With a dopamine deficit i need shows and youtube videos basically any kind of entertainment to get to a point where i can actually function, otherwise theres just this painful boredom.  After taking medication i didnt NEED entertainment to function, i finally realised entertainment isnt supposed to be the only thing that can give u just enough to actually get through the day. Its just some extra fun. Neurotypicals dont NEED it to get by its just nice to have  Ive never truly enjoyed a lot of things, ive recognised they are fun but my sense of fun is warped, ive lived thinking "fun" is being able to get to that baseline of finally being able to function, its never really felt GOOD its just allowed me to make it through the day  But with medication im already at that baseline if not above it and i finally realise all that was wrong. Entertainment wasnt designed for me i needed it to go above and beyond to properly feel happy because of something (hyperfixation) but most things aren't interesting enough to do that  ENA knows that all of this is "fun" but its just not enough or it doesnt feel right, she feels left out of it because she understands its fun but it doesnt FEEL fun for her  Not sure if i explained this very well but its 2am so yknow  I might make another comment some time properly analysing this episode. this is something small and i might be misremembering it but there was an earlier version of the indonesian subtitle where moony said the "ring, rong, run" part, and the person who wrote the translated caption made their own version into "bel, bal, bablas". i thought it was already clever in that version even though the word "bablas" directly translates to "babble" but we can loosely or casually use it in other different context (i.e. running hastily). while it's helpful to give somewhat of a translated explanation in the captions and not to discredit the translator as well, but i wished the charm in the original version stayed as someone who had become a bit weary in seeing stiff and formal indonesian subtitles in media :"{  - love, a (nitpicky) indonesian ENA fan

I'm also thinking it has to do with going through your life, or maybe just your "golden years". act 1 represents falling through the beginning of it, hitting your head as you fall into place, eventually coming out of the twisting pipes of figuring out where you will be, the crying ladies saying they're happy is similar to how people say they enjoy their job or life, but clearly are misrible. act 2 could be a continuation of this interpretation, going with the flow and feeling "happy and joy" or that you belong, but you really don't. either you arent as happy as they are, or no one is and its just everyone faking. you don't fit in with the normal of everyone else.  i saw act three as dying, it being the crecendo of the decent. looking back at your life and going through the motions of living and accomplishments, but you didn't enjoy it. life is a chore, you didn't enjoy any of it. it was painful and dull. everyone else sees it as a miracle, but all you see it as is a painful dance where nothing makes sense and you just arent a part of it.  the skull face makes a bit more sense to me, its the realisation that life isn't meant to be fun. it isn't naturally kind to you, it isn't normally fun. its IS a painful dance through it, but you can still find joy and fun in the little moments, you just have to look for it.  the blue mask feels to me like masking and lying to oneself to hide your true feelings. i think. it leads you through life, staying at the forefront, pretending to be what you arent to make things easier, as ena often agrees with it and follows it along through this theater of life, until the realisation and self reflection of how she really feels, thus destroying the mask.  for the ending I have nothing. i thought it was gonna be her seeing the joy in having friends, but then things happened and idk  or something idk, I feel like I'm completely wrong, but art is meant to be interpreted so yeah. no clue.

As someone with depression this is my interpretation of the episode: As you know, ENA has two sides, one that is sad (blue w/ female voice) and one that has a more positive attitude (yellow w/ male voice). In this episode she puts on a mask to hide her sad side, and creates a fa√ßade, pretending to be cheerful, trying to "buy" happiness, but she is never truly experiencing joy. In the first act, she also realizes that as much as she tries to, she cannot become cheerful through connecting with other people. In the third and fourth act she is literally putting on an act to other people and herself. Only when she goes to therapy in the last act she drops the fa√ßade, and realizes that what makes other people 'happy' (the crying statue, for example), isn't going to make her happy as well. The skull thingy sees right through her, and then explains to her that she has to find enjoyment in small things.

My summary of each act (sorry if it sounds weird): ACT 1: Display The actor puts on a mask to display themselves as a jolly fellow and to join in the play.  ACT 2: The Rising Despite following the exact script, they slowly start to get some rising confusion as to why they aren‚Äôt feeling the same joy as everyone else, as if they can‚Äôt fit in.  ACTs 3 & 4: Crescendo of a Descent. The start of the downfall. The actor realises that (despite feeling audience gratification) there‚Äôs absolutely nothing jollifying in this play to begin with, nothing that they like at all, and the mask slowly starts to slip off.  ACT 5: Therapy With some help, the mask is broken, and the patient accepts the fact that they don‚Äôt need to force themselves to always take part in major things such as a play to feel joy, thus completing their resolution.

one of my favorite interpretations of this episode is that its an allegory for autism. ena tries to find joy in activities that others enjoy, but she herself finds strange or tiresome; something i experience frequently as an autistic person myself.  Act I: Connections and bonds that are meant to transmit cheerfulness do not necessarily transmit happiness to Ena when she tries to connect with them. Similarly, a decent chunk of folks with autism find that they aren‚Äôt truly integrated into their friendships and are merely tolerated. Not joy is being transmitted, just tolerance.  Act II: ‚ÄúSometimes, the most astonishing experiences are the ones we never expect.‚Äù As Ena‚Äôs mask puts it, this strain of joy is exploring the unknown. It‚Äôs an endless stream of change and Ena simply doesn‚Äôt get it. As twists and turns become unfamiliar, routine is broken and that‚Äôs an uncomfortable feeling for some folks. They have a different rhythm and waltzing off beat is odd.  Act III & IV: What is a story of silent movements if not body language and facial cues? While Ena is capable of acting out these silent movements and is praised for doing so, it‚Äôs something that‚Äôs only tiring. Ena doesn‚Äôt sense any change in who she is, and is only acting out a role she didn‚Äôt mean to play.  Act V: This one is just self-evident. This is the one part where Ena‚Äôs mask breaks off, and the therapist calls its joy ‚Äúexaggerated‚Äù, adding to the idea that the mask is her masking her sadness. She understands how it‚Äôs supposed to make her happy, but she can‚Äôt feel that happiness. The therapist tells her that she won‚Äôt find any fulfillment in the building, as it‚Äôs a place not built for her.  what does the end mean? I Cannot Tell You.

Through each room we see Blue signifying her optimistic and passionate outlook on art ("Wowie! I'd like to buy some of those"). Yellow behaves realistically in contrast, like shes us reflecting on the room before her. Blue doesnt, she sees art objectively like a how an art connoisseur does -- detached yet intrigued like a true observer.  In the end we see she's not a part of Ena anymore. She's the mask.  I believe in the scheme of my theory, this signifies art's loss of its sense of self, especially the subject matter Ena represents. Maybe she's a representation of all of art's audiences. When you are the audience, everything can just be a skip and a glance to you. You can pause, you can reflect, but you are eventually on your way. Random thought but y'know how ENA seems to be struggling to find satisfaction or happiness in all of these episodes (with her trying to achieve a goal as a form of happiness achievement or purpose)?  You think Moony, despite her confident and brash exterior, is also struggling to find happiness/satisfaction in her own way?  One of the key details about Moony's design is the big square shaped hole in her face, which is always carrying something different in it- as anything that goes in never stays forever. It's like she's trying to fill a void in herself (literally, but perhaps also metaphorically) but the pieces she tries to put in there do not fit (or she herself ends up throwing them away, like she did with the red piece in this episode).  Moony is also shown to be very willing to grab/steal things that belong to other people in order to fill the hole, such as the zipper guy's...guy at the end of this episode, or the Shepherdess' staff + a mannequin person's limb in Temptation Stairway. Maybe she's willing to steal things from other people to fill the void, in hopes that the things that make other people happy/complete will make her happy/complete?  ENA's search for happiness is shown in a very emotion/character based way, but she's also our focus character- perhaps Moony's own search for happiness is also happening in the background, never shown emotionally since Moony acts so brashly outwardly, but rather in Moony's actions  ENA and Moony also both lose critical details of their designs in the finale of Temptation Stairway: ENA's body becomes entirely yellow (losing her iconic two-toned palette- losing the blue side of her that represents sadness), while Moony's entire old design is lost when she develops a humanoid body that barely resembles her old self (and lacks the square hole she's always trying to fill)- and these are both implied to be the combined results of a wish to the Great Runas and the winner of their race paying the debts of the loser (a wish that would presumably give the winner/wisher happiness, and repaying the debts of the loser would presumably also give the loser happiness)  I dunno...maybe that's just a bunch of nonsense but just a shower thought I had XD

I think that all of these acts may be in relation to, well relationships (not just romantic to be clear), and ENA as a very likely representation of depression (or neurodivergence) trying to tackle them.  Act 1 is the connections themselves, considered by many to feel satisfying and meaningful just by their existence, but ENA can't see the point in connection alone.  Act 2 is the the twists and turns of interaction with people, the happy surprises and the conflicts. I think this is why the act looks like it does, it's walking the streets of life with other faces along side you. ENA however is off put by their lives and problems, and/or (could be both) rather the people around ENA don't understand or click with them.  Act 3 & 4 I believe is putting on an act for those around you, and feeling the acts they put on themselves (or possibly 4 is the satisfaction from their approval in your act). I feel like the character's appearances in this act reinforce that; skeletons that can't express much masquerading behind these thin cut-outs that show how they want to be seen. ENA knows how to put on an act often quite well, but doesn't feel like they gain anything from it, it feels like a chore, a job.  Act 5 is what you're usually pointed to when you have these troubles, Therapy (as its clearly stated). The therapist points out their mask's exaggeration and ENA opens up, realizing that to go through this play (the game of relationships) they've worn a mask that covers the side of themself they dislike. The mask always seems to "get" the point of each play, but in a very superficial way, like it's pretending to understand and enjoy it. I think the next bit is basically the therapist telling ENA that they don't HAVE to be chasing relationships to enjoy life, and can just find fun in the simple things you're not usually made to consider. That's maybe why at the end ENA comments that the play (representing relationships in theory) wasn't very fun, and is so perplexed by the strange behaviors and abrasive nature of Moony, which I feel like ENA usually doesn't question in an attempt to fit the mold of standard relationships.  Thank you for coming to my Ted Talk :)

I saw this as ENA taking a journey through the Internet itself. At the end when Moony told ENA that she was supposed to ring the bell and run, I saw that as we're not really supposed to get addicted to the internet and expect it to be fun, rather we're supposed to take short glimpses and then put the device down (ringing the bell = taking a look, running = setting it down). Here's how I saw each individual act:  Act 1 (Display): This is the top layer, when you're starting out on your dive into the web. It doesn't exactly make sense, but it's still fascinating. Therefore, you're compelled to keep going deeper. Act 2 (The Rising): This is the joy of finding something that you find interesting, but at the same time you're confused by it. So, in an attempt to understand it you delve deeper and deeper until you struggle to get out. Act 3 & 4 (Crescendo of a Descent): Once you get deep enough you'll eventually wind up interacting with the community itself, and you're compelled to join them in the activities they partake in, which may wind up being content creation for the community. You end up accruing your own small gathering, and eventually that gathering grows into your own fan base. Sadly, their constant need for more content means you need to churn out content more and more until it stops being a joy and turns into a chore. You barely even interact with the fan base anymore, aside from the required creator-community interactions. Your life becomes a tale of silent movements that you either like alot or don't like at all, which inevitably leads to... Act 5 (Therapy): I see this as finally coming to terms that what you're doing isn't healthy in the slightest. You accept that it may be in the best interest to take a break, and that's what you do. You take the break, perhaps coming back or perhaps not, and eventually you leave the Internet. You reach a resolution.

ENA, in my eyes, is becoming more and more of  the dichotomy of emotion and logic. in the past, though blue may have always been rather down, she kept the character grounded, while yellow excels at interacting with and understanding the logic of world.  we got to see their inherent flaws from time to time through blues various breakdowns, and yellow not making sense of various actions, but here, they are both so far removed from their respective element that their flaws shine right on through.   blue is quite literally masking the whole episode and pretending to be joyful, while yellow is way too logical to even comprehend what joy is supposed to be. and both of them in the end struggle with the same subject and find a sense of unity in this. like the therapist said, they both have to enjoy the little moments, even if the moments are too small for blue, and even if yellow may not understand these feelings.

I've been thinking about this a lot since it was released. I wonder how much of it is a reflection of Joel's own experience with fame from Extinction Party, Temptation Stairway, and the to-be-released game on Steam. It's not uncommon to achieve ones goals and then not feel the way we expected to feel, or even experience anhedonia--like what ENA seems to be going through here. The line, "It's now your mission" could refer to the pressure to keep performing at a high level after receiving such outstanding praise for previous passion projects. And, "Though I feel the gratification of the audience, I can't sense any change in me" might be almost literal.

Something I just noticed is that Ena repeats one pose thrice in this short.  The first time is when greeting the bunny, the second when asking the shadow kids for directions to the next Act, and the last is the first time Happy Ena speaks after the Mask is destroyed.  In these scenes, Mask and Happy Ena are looking in opposite directions, helping sell that Mask isn‚Äôt representative of Ena's true self. But in the third one, Sad and Happy are both looking in the same direction, indicating that Ena's being more true to herself.  Also, since the first two times the pose comes up are with meeting people for the first time, it could be interpretted that the third time is her more properly greeting the therapist since the therapist appeared literally out of nowhere and Ena's now greeting him with her genuine self.

the way I interpret it, this is about living with depression and each act is meant to represent common beliefs on how to derive happiness or purpose in life.   Act 1: Joy through social connections, love of friends and family   Act 2: Joy through exploring the world and learning new things   Act 3 and 4: Joy through serving others   Act 5, Therapy: Though these things may work for others, continually forcing yourself into them with the expectation that they Should make you happy too will only make you more miserable.  Forget about trying to find deeper meaning in nonsense. Instead, find happiness in life‚Äôs little moments- hearing your favorite song, eating something delicious, witnessing a sunrise. These are small moments of joy, but they are joy still.

ENA! It‚Äôs wonderful to see them again! I thoroughly enjoyed the video and got my own theories on everything including what the acts represent. It is clear ENA is searching for fun and happiness in this place, and it equates to how many strive to be happy in their own lives. There are many different views on how one can achieve this and they are represented in the video through various acts. The mask analysis has been done to death in the comments so I‚Äôll be analyzing the acts.  ACT I: DISPLAY (The joy of connection and consumption) The connections of this area may represent connections one may make with others. Whether over the internet or in real life, relationships with friends and family bring joy to many. The area may also be representative of seeing what others can provide you through their own creations that they may share such as images and movies.  ACT II: THE RISING (The joy of existence) The symbolism gets deeper and I may be more philosophical with this one. Through one‚Äôs journey in finding happiness in life, some may find peace and happiness in simply existing and experiencing life through all of its ups and downs. After all, we only get one. The prospect of the unknown future can be exiting. The world will continue whether you‚Äôre having fun or not, will you be content following its rhythm?  ACT III and IV: CRESCENDO OF A DESCENT (The joy of creating and serving) While the two acts are in the same section, I think they are significantly different. To feel joy by serving others or showing them things that bring them happiness feels much different to feeling joy from the process of making something on your own and enjoying your own creation. One serves others while the other is self serving. These acts may coincide with each other since some find creating for others as their source of happiness in life.  ACT V: THERAPY (A last resort) This one is pretty straight forward. In a search for happiness many people seek professional help on the matter. I do think there is significance in this one being the final act we see, as a lot of the time therapy is only considered after someone has tried everything to find happiness by themselves to no avail. Remember, it‚Äôs alright to seek outside help. You‚Äôre not alone in this quest for happiness. Even if therapy doesn‚Äôt work out it doesn‚Äôt mean it‚Äôs the end. Everyone has their own way to have fun, and there‚Äôs nothing wrong if you don‚Äôt enjoy a certain activity. Just be patient and keep trying out new things.   Thank you for reading! I may type out more in depth stuff like line analyses and my own take on the mask symbolism if people show interest.

Êó•Êú¨Ë™ûË®≥„ÅåÊ¨≤„Åó„ÅÑ„Åß„Åô ‰ªä„Åæ„Åß„Å®„ÅØ‰Ωï„Åã„ÅåÈÅï„ÅÜÊ∞ó„Åå„Åô„Çã
Some thoughts on this wonderful episode.  This seems to be a clear continuation of some sort to Temptation Stairway. Remember how ENA seemed even more overwhelmed than usual in that ep? Even to the point of being downright suicidal with some of the comments she made... and at the very end, once they've seemingly reached the Runas, her blue side has suddenly disappeared. It makes me think that the wish that ENA made was to get rid of her sadness, finding it too much to bear. But as Ulysses warned her... desires are never fulfilled nor quenched.  So she hasn't gotten rid of her problems, not really. She's just literally 'masked' them now. And as a result of this repression, even her happy side isn't as bright as it used to be - now more passive and doubtful, downright confused on how, no matter how much she searches for happiness, it seems so far out of reach now. She feels utterly out of place in this world that she used to fit right into, even if it overwhelmed her at times. Because how can you feel connected to what's around you if you don't even feel connected to yourself?  And while that's all obvious enough - I wanted to try and theorize a bit on the different acts here, too, and what they mean.  Before the acts even start, we meet the Bunny, who says "What a stink! That is not the essence of merriness... aren't you entertained enough?" Irl, there's plenty of people who make comments like that towards depressed people. _What's with the long face? Why aren't you happy? You have everything you need, right? Your life is good, right? Quit moping, you're bringing the mood down..._ and sentiments along the sort. That's just what that made me think of.  Now, the first act is a bunch of pipes connecting - "Connections and bonds that are meant to transmit cheerfulness", as ENA puts it. And the immediate first thing that came to my mind, both from the visuals and the wording, are... the neural pathways in our brains. Whatever is wrong with ENA, it's obviously neurological, as all mental illnesses/disorders are, and it's not something that you can just 'think' away. There is something legitimately different in your brain. "I don't recognize this strain of joy."  Before the second act, we meet the lady in the wall, who is crying. ENA, almost accusatory, asks her "aren't you supposed to be cheering?", as if she has come to believe that emotions, the 'bad' ones at least, are a inherently, well... bad. And the lady just replies that these tears are from joy, and that this happiness isn't one that can be bought. I think this represents what it's like to truly be able to experience your emotions in full - unembarrassed, and not caused by anything like drugs or any other addictions... just fully so happy you could cry. But, of course, ENA can't understand that concept yet.  Which we see in the second act - the one that supposedly made the lady that happy, and one that ENA can't comprehend at all. "Am I the one the rhythm can't catch?" _Am I just the odd one out here?_ If we're stretching the metaphors, we could also extrapolate that the mask's line of "the entire universe is waltzing with me" has a sort of meaning of feeling connected to the world around you and stuff... and I could try to explain what the visuals mean, but that might be digging too far even for me, lol. Important thing is, again, ENA struggles to find joy in things others can.  The third and fourth act, is a "story of silent movements." A performance. I think this represents ENA trying to go along and _pretend_ to be happy even if she can't feel it inside. Maybe if she just looks the part, if she gives out something to the world, it'll help, right? But... "Though I feel the gratification of the audience, I can't feel any change in me." She can try to be happy for others, but she _can't_ fake it 'till she makes it, not on this. All that it makes her realize is, in contrast, how miserable she feels deep down.  "Hey... how could a chore like this jollify someone, anywho?"  That's all that this is to her, at this point. A chore - anything that seems fun just feels like a chore to her now. This could be many things - art, performing, eating, waking up in the morning, meeting with friends... when you're depressed, things that would bring you joy normally no longer do, and you're left just cruising, forcing yourself into things. And that can be... very tiring.  Notice how the mask falls, when she says that. She's finally out of her denial.  And then she, quite _literally,_ goes to therapy LMAO  Which, the fifth act speaks for itself, I think, and this comment is already WAYY too long so I'll just end it here lol If anyone actually read this - hi and have a virtual cookie, thank you üç™  Gosh this series is amazing <3

This art style is gorgeous but somehow it just makes me feel... afraid. Is that normal? LOL
I think i have a reason for why ena gets weirded out and confused in her weird world.  Ena is a creature of symbolic recognition, like humans. She can pick up similar symbols and make meaning of them. Yet she lives in a world where that really doesn't matter much, or at the very least not in the same way she (and we) does.   Other entities in this realm have similar patterns that they do and range in how much they can pick up patterns, but nowhere near as much as ena can. Moony, who has at least enough symbol recognition to understand the worlds rules and recognize when ena is somehow acting up, is on the higher end of the spectrum. Its probably why shes enas best friend. Yet her symbol recognition is more premade, sculpted to react to the world she lives in. Unlike ena who can constantly analyze and cross analyze any new symbols.   Entities like the moderator at the beginning of episode 2 lack almost all symbol recognition, depending of a more computer binary thinking to know yes or no answers to problems. Yet it has a way of acting thats of this world not necessarily in binary thinking, but as an organic creature.  Ena may have spent her whole life here getting used to this world and understanding its patterns. but again, pattern recognition is not very valuable here. So she does her best to act in accordance with the world. Its all shes known. This may be why she has 2 beings. She developed a split personality to try and cope with the stresses she has. Yet when things confuse her, she gets triggered by it. And how she reacts can depend on what personality shes embodying. When shes yellow ena, she will show expressions of true confusion, or shell start getting euphoric and glitch out like the end of ep 2. When shes sad, she can be sent into a panic attack, like in the beginning of episode 3. Her mask may also be a form of coping of the randomness for her sad side, but im still piecing together whether that fits with this episodes themes of joy. The closest thing i can think of right now is that she's trying to find happiness in this world she's incapable of fully comprehending.  If this is right, this raises more questions about this universe. What is ena then? Is she human? Is this world a computer program? Or perhaps its more of a psychedelic realm something Terrance mckenna would talk about? And what exactly is the logic of this world and the grander story being unraveled here? So many questions that make me super excited for what comes next for the series!  EDIT: after a few rewatches, I think I got a better idea of the mask and the symbol recognition.   The mask was not only a coping attempt for the weirdness of the world, but also a hope to achieve an idea of fun, joy and happiness that only her yellow side is fully familiar with. Blue ena has a self hatred for herself in a way that overwhelms her entire being. Yet even in that state, he knows about her happy side. That feeling of happiness is something she deeply wants and is tired of lapsing into dangerous levels of depression. And at the end of episode 3, where she becomes entirely yellow, the idea of the mask came to her. A mask that would have her always be as happy as yellow.  The mask works in a way that tries to have her blue side emulate her yellow, at least in action and appearance. While it can't remove her depressed aspects of herself, it can at least repress them. And instead of being disturbed by the nonsensicalness of the world, she just tries to roll with it.  Yet in the very process of attempting of being fully happy, her yellow side in fact becomes less happy. Where sad ena used to occur more when things disturbed her or made no sense, the happy ena was there instead because of the mask. So when she tried to be happy when she ought not to be, the confusion and realization she has no idea what's going on grew and grew. Even the entities is the place recognized she was abysmal even if she couldnt.  The skull therapist is perhaps the character with the most symbolic recognition outside of ena, and seems to have and understanding of how the ena's work (all of them, not just blue and yellow). While he may not have full symbolic recognition, he has enough to know how to help her. That being to tell her that lying to herself about how sad she is will make things worse and she'll never find happiness by fully embracing the most abstract places in her world.   Ena at her happiest are indeed in the little moments. Like giving a gift to moony or enjoying the serenity of the runas resting place. Like it or not, this nonsensical world is enas home. And the sooner she can accept the harder aspects of living there, the sooner she can have more fun.

My interpretation is that every act except the last is a representation of the stages of life where we find joy. The first in connections or friendships, the second in work or promotions and finally sharing the experience of your life with younger people as you get older. Finally, the only solution was to go to therapy and discover that it is impossible to have joy all the time... And although we convince ourselves and others with a mask of happiness, we must understand that pain is organic and exists so that there is joy.

Headcanon: This happened all in Ena's mind after making her wish to the great Runas, eliminating her blue side, and whenever Ena says "CHEESE AND RICE MOONY" she's not referring to Moony turning into a bipedal person, she's referring to Moony's brutality in dragging the random ass being through their square hole. Right after she says that, she goes back to where she actually is. The concept of fun and happiness is her internal monologue of having to get rid of her bad side. The Runas grants wishes, but the wishes require Ena to *learn" the concept of fun and enter it into her being. She has made many wishes before, and has even tried to do it herself, which is why skeleguy says "You have been here many times before. You need not return here. This is your resolution." effectively getting rid of her blue bad side. The mask is a metaphor for Ena trying to cover up her blue side by trying to act happy and "normal" (As normal as Ena could be in her very screwed up world), and her referring to it as a "Lousy mask" shows how tired she is of covering it up. She simply just wants to get rid of it.  But yeah. I think too much about things that really have no meaning.

All the episode analyses in the comments here are great and all, but I think people are neglecting the importance of the mask. Sure, it's Ena's sad side, but dig a little deeper. It's *eating* her sad side, and it's talking all happy. I think we can derive Ena's wish from the Great Runas from this, to always have fun. Ena often gets in the way of her own fun with her wild mood swings. But, desires are never fulfilled nor quenched. The mask is a veneer of happiness. One that finally breaks at the end. I think Ena is a representation of bipolar disorder, maybe. Before, Ena swung between a manic side (yellow) and a depressed side (blue). But by removing the depressed side, when Ena was done being manic and off the walls like she normally is, she's left just... I hesitate to say normal but, I guess just, dull. And then she managed to find her way back to depression. Though, less sad and more... Nothing. And it's in this state we follow her through the episode. Actual clinical depression. She tries desperstely to find that joy, to feel happiness again. But it's forced. It's a mask literally made of her depression. It's only by accepting the sadness as part of her that she's... Probably feeling back to normal? I guess we'll see in another 5000 years when Joel G blesses us with another episode.
Nothing has quite captured the feeling I used to get from point-and-click adventure games as a kid in the late 90s so much as ENA. It's so perfectly surreal in atmosphere.
This episode feels like a commentary on masking mental illness and therapy. It might be obvious but I'm no Sherlock so I'm glad I noticed that at least

8:30 FNAF REFERENCE OR SMTH
As someone who was born in the year 2000, but played a lot of 'retro' games when I was little I get a strange nostalgia form watching this, not only because of the graphics, but also the writing, as a lot of the games that I used to play where in English or Japanese, neither of which are my native language. Reading the dialogue in ENA and trying to fully make sense of it feels a lot like how it felt to do the same with those games when I was so young, I could barely read my native language, let alone English. Not that the writing is bad, no, quite the opposite in fact.  I hope to see more of this series in the future. (·µî·¥•·µî)

This one definitely feels creepier than all the other episodes, It seems to exude a bit of a depressing aura which I believe its what they were going for. It seems sparse like a party that has just ended.  I wonder if there is a metaphor here for finding meaning throughout one's life. First, young people find meaning through seeking out new experiences (represented by the film girl in the wall), then later in psychosocial development people often attempt to settle down into a role and find meaning in doing things for others. (As eluded to by the shadow children and the skeletons.) Towards the end of one's lifetime, death nears which seems to be a theme with all of the skulls present.   This is just my guess, however. I'm not sure if this wonderful piece of art should be interpreted in the first place.

4:30 Acts III & IV seem to reference Plato's Allegory of the Cave, more specifically the Crescendo of a Descent into said cave. In his allegory, "The Cave", Plato describes a group of people who have lived chained to the wall of a cave all their lives, facing a blank wall. The people watch shadows projected on the wall from objects passing in front of a fire behind them and give names to these shadows. The shadows are the prisoners' reality, but are not accurate representations of the real world. The shadows represent the fragment of reality that we can normally perceive through our senses, while the objects under the sun represent the true forms of objects that we can only perceive through reason. The audience may find joy in the entertaining distraction created by the show of shadows, and that audience includes the actors themselves along with the entirety of humanity. They take comfort in the shadows, for in the shadows, they may acknowledge figments of enjoyment and pleasure without ever facing their incomprehensible feelings.

The vibe I get from this one is that this can be a metaphor for "masking", a term used to describe people on the autism spectrum who attempt to hide signature characteristics of the disorder. Most notably the mask is kinda... parasitic in design, and seemingly has "locked" the blue 'side' of ENA, which is notably the side that is prone to meltdowns and behavior that Moony has treated as more rude and annoying. 'Blue' doesn't come back until after the weird 'link' combining the two is severed, and then she is quite open about her negative emotions.   Overall, very nice video, I absolutely love the designs, the mask itself, the weird chopped up bunny thing, the weird skulls therapist thing is cool, and I love the 'overworld' animations kinda resembling more of a strange 3D third person game (another notable detail about the mask is that it kinda "leads" ENA in certain directions.)

My interpretation is that after temptation stairway, instead of getting rid of her sad face, she just manages to conceal it on a mask that mimics happiness while literally chewing her depresive antisocial self. She tries to have fun, but fail's to understand what is about. In act I, she doesn't get how funny actions and the amazement you get from them are supposed to give you "fun", on act II she understands that people flow along with that "fun", and while her mask pretends to have fun alongside them, inside she doesn't understand where's the "fun", to her all the expresions remain bored. On act III she becomes the source of "fun" to the audience, showing a funny silhouette while her inside remains dead, and act IV is about how, even though she gets pleasure from the audience's praise, she can't get the fun she's been looking for, finally breaking, her mask no longer concealing her sad side In act V her mask is desperately trying to hide her evident sadness, and once she gets therapy, she destroys her mask and aknowledge that she just can't feel fun.  To summarize, I think the mask is a representation of her denying and concealing all her sadness and atempting to live a 100% fun life, but in the process she lost the meaning of what "fun" is supossed to mean. in the end, "fun" trully is precious when it's in balance with sadness, is it's scarcity what gives it it's value.  Or perhaps, ENA's weird and has no repair, I'll have to rewatch the video a couple dozen times just in case i missed something. Babe wake up, new ena just posted
It's a big theme throughout the video that she's masking her sad side, quite literally with a physical mask. I think there's a little bit more to it than just that though.   The way I see it, it explores simple pleasures, more intricately drug abuse.   I think Act II is showing the actual high of drugs, mostly because of ENA becoming part of the set. People who have experienced psychedelics have talked about becoming different objects. ENA starts by describing it as a strange happiness, but as the vision fades disturbing imagery appears within the dark starry background. The transition of euphoria to anxiety can be assorted with the long term use of drugs, and how the high degrades over time.   Because of this, I think Act I is previous users talking about their experience with hallucinogens to ENA. This could be them getting ENA initially hooked on drug abuse, especially with the line, "Rather, The Second Act granted me this ecstasy." They're encouraging ENA to try it.   I don't think Act III and VI are much about drugs, unlike the previous acts. I think it's about art as a more reasonable means of individual discovery.   The performers are depicted as shadows before skeletons. The shadow is a basic outline of a person, while the skeleton is dead and unlifelike. While the skeleton on it's own would have no meaning, the shadow brings it movement and emotion. In a way, it could be argued that the performers represent giving life to art, even beyond the grave. The performers encourage ENA to enjoy this moment.   The reason Act III and VI are placed in the same segment is, in my opinion, because of how ENA reacts to the performers.   "Though I feel the gratification of the audience, I can't sense any change in me. Hey, how could a chore like this jollify someone anywho?"  ENA has affinity for praise, but has no interest in the art itself. In a way, it could be interpreted as the art killing the artist. When art is monetized it can easily become less gratifying to create, and lose it's freedom. ENA reaps the reward of creating but mourns the loss of creation.   Act V is exactly how it seems, ENA is on the road to recovery. She vents her frustrations about wearing a mask, which is obvious symbolism of the mask of forced joy we use daily. The skulls say to ENA, "You have been coming here persistently, over and over. The truth is though, you will never find fun in this place." To me this wraps up the themes of Act I and II. He's telling her that consistent abuse of substances will only bring her more misery. This is also further noted with the quote, "You need not return here anymore. This is your resolution."  "Fun is quite the illusive varmint. But remember, it is never lost forever. Often, the greatest fun can be found in the true moments." They're telling ENA to live in the moment.   To me, this video is symbolic of using quick pleasures to fill the void solemn emotions leave. The solution in the end is to finally cut free from simple quick fixes, and organically find Fun. ENA explores this by enjoying life after the five acts, playing Ring Rong Run with Moony and the unnamed enigma.

You know, I don't know if it's just because the subtext was so blatant you could call it text, or if I've simply seen enough surrealist art to just *get* it, OR if I've secretly developed depression that suddenly makes me catch these sorts of stories, but this is the first ENA short I really... Get. Empathize with. Understand.  Now, don't get me wrong, I love Auction Day, Extinction Party, and Temptation Stairway. I think they're all brilliant animations that are simply fascinating. But the stories they tell, at least to my recollection, are simply fun romps across wild and wacky worlds meant to just deliver a "wow" factor. For sure, there are underlying messages to all of them that reveal aspects of ENA's character and establish an arc for the series as a whole, but they feel so... Missable, to my knowledge. I'll admit that it's been a while since I've seen them, and they probably merit a rewatch, but those underlying elements have always just sort of escaped me in favor of the absurd world and cast of characters.  But this one, man. This one hits different. And yeah, the literal Therapist (amazing vocal performance to their voice actor btw) is PROBABLY what makes this one so easy to understand, as well as those underlying arcs finally coming to a head with ENA finally at odds with herself to some extent. Wanting to get rid of/"heal" her sad half with a mask which inevitably breaks, the way she goes through the play over and over again but never finds the joy in it everyone else seems to and considers it a chore, having to learn to find joy in all of the little moments... As a young adult, I suddenly *get* what that feels like. This simply abstract series of random mishaps just spoke to me when I least expected it to - and that's what makes this episode my favorite.  Y'know, barring the amazing animation, aesthetic, voice work, humor, and everything else that automatically makes this short peak internet animation. That also helps it, I'd say.

WE UP
At first it seemed to me that the episode was a critique of content creation on the internet, performing for an audience while extracting no pleasure or value from the craft itself, everything just a game of anonymous faces behind masks of fun and pleasure. Now looking at the comments, I think the premise can be broadened to modern society in general, how we see social interaction as a strange mix between self protection and mutual pleasure, scared to open up and scared to be left behind. This is probably especially true of the world and even more so the internet during the COVID era, where people were practicaly forced to bygo any form of wholesome interaction and digitize all forms of social activity. Our society is one that seeks fun over wellbeing and inner peace, for we are so plagued by issues that we cannot see any avenues of change; we shrink away and put on a mask, hoping to be spared from the plague of depression and loneliness which consumes us each like a beast manifested from our anxious self-obsessions. Good episode, definitely worth a re-watch.

So I think fun isn't actually what ENA is looking for. I think ENA Is looking for meaning and community. The acts are telling:  Act 1: Endless connection, illusion and delusion meant to *transmit* joy. Perhaps this is referring to the Internet and/or conspiracy theorist culture. Either seems to fit. Either we are in a world of delusions and illusions where everything is connected and a shadowy cabal is behind everything or we are in conspiracy theorist territory. Meaning and community don't last here.  Act 2:  The Rising where the universe dances in oneness. This sounds like religion of some kind, chasing the transcendent, rising upward to heaven and union with others. This is simply too strange for even ENA.  4-5 Nihilism.  Meaning is a shadow, a play we put on. We act as though there is meaning and attempt to create it on our own but it's all merely a shadow barely concealing mortal bodies doomed to die.  5: A big face made of skulls. ENA confronts the reality of death. Our time in this life os limited. We can only do our best to find community and meaning and love not in grand narratives and philosophies but in the small moments. Then ENA is spat out to mert her friend. It's just them two and the weird dog creature but it is with these little people closest to us that we can find real meaning and community.

I was not expecting gmod ragdoll sounds, that caught me off guard.  .. OH, right, the digital philosophy.. Alright! Let me dive in!  As per my previous take on this series, I divulged that it seemed like a pretty cut-and-dry scenario aping that of those old online make-your-own-world type games, except everyone stopped dying and the servers stayed around for eternity, creating a virtually infinite realm of nonsensical pocket-dimensions with non-euclidean pathways and whimsical characters!  And in this episode, it would seem ena has lost her way, and became briefly caught up in the reasoning behind it all.. Was there not a point to these worlds, their creation and its contents? Ah yes, "fun", that was it! Except, without all of these world's hosts around to explain the geometry or characters, the universe has such a hollow and benign feel to it.. Not very fun.. But alas, she is reminded by an old friend that fun is always around.. You just have to find it! And if you cannot find it, you MAKE it.. Fun isn't always the act of creation, but rather A creation, a machination of a bored mind wishing and yearning for stimulation and chaos!  As always, the points on display hit the nail on the head, and the view is quite refreshing too! I appreciate this, and look forward to whatever comes out next!

This show may sound absurd but it's really representative. This reminds me of my "resolution" when it came to appreciating the little things and the unexpected events in my life (that will never happen again). An odd sense of consuming nostalgia (that paradoxically haunts me insteading of cheers me sometimes), coupled with a severe case of optimism, never served me well. I'm happy acknowledging that the joy I feel right now comes from things long gone from time and memory, leaving behind just impressions, just as will do what's happening in my life right now in the future. Life is absurd with all of its "joyful" and "depressing" moments that we decide they are so. There has been moments in my life where I just don't understand how or what to feel, or why, moments where I get confused; The world we live in is irrational, and the true sense of joy comes with accepting that fact, whilst we are sad when we refuse to accept that unchangeable fact and look for a better well suited explanation and meaning in a missmatched world, whilst relying on our inconsistent and opposing senses/memory and self.

I have a theory on the meaning of the acts i think these are meant to represent sources of entertainment and the gratification they bring Act 1 Display: is about conection, ilusion and delusion, i think these simbolize interacting with other people, maintaining a facade for others, pretend to care for them as they pretend to care for you Ena doesnt find joy in talking with others yet the mask is happy to perform a display Act 2 The Rising: this one is kinda subjetive but i believe the blue crying ladys with projector on their eyes are a clue, this is an exploration into the unknown so i believe this is any type of escapism that you could have in your life Movies, Books, Videogames, Series, etc Ena can't seem to catch the rythm of the things others find entertaining or popular Act 3 and 4 Crecendo of a Descent: this one i believe is the most obvious it is a methaphor of life itself all of us are growing old we have a descent into death, Ena is already a performer in this grand act, our time is limited every moment is precious and Ena should be enjoying her life yet, she cant find joy in every day chores, "life is work not fun" this presents a disconection between herself and the mask Because she can fool others but not herself, she can't pretend to care for life all the time and starts doubting how any of this is meant to bring joy which allows for an oportunity Act 5 Therapy: once Ena has realized that she and the mask are not the same finds the strenght to go to therapy, the therapist explains that Life is a joy that she cannot yet understand, the mask tries to pretend everything is fine and she is having fun yet this facade feels off once the therapist calls her out for it Ena introspect and open up to show her true feelings, once she does this she doesnt need to pretend to like or enjoy things that don't amuse her, be true to herself and enjoy the little things that do bring her joy, that is okey to not feel happy or entertained all the time her resolution comes to full effect once Moony ask how the fun house was and she gives an honest opinion Ena has been trasnformed by this experience but not in the way she wanted to, she wanted to "feel like she is suppose to" but now she can truly accept that she doesn't and thats okey she can feel whatever and its okey

this episode is a very well-done one. and what i like about it is how it allows the viewer to have many interpretations. in this journey, ena shows a very empty and depressed part of herself. the whole episode she's trying to find "fun," but i think what suits better is something like happiness or joy, and even so, ena seems to not be achieving that happiness. in many moments during this video, it's shown how she can't find that joy and she can't comprehend it (to be specific, 2:03 "and even so I...don't recognize this strain of joy" and 5:21 "I can't sense any change in me"). pretty much while everyone was being amused by the acts in the theater, by different ways & reactions, ena stood the same.  one specific part that I really liked was the realization that she wasn't really happy, on 5:21. the mask, which was by her side through this whole episode, dragging her, attached to her face, and is represented, specifically in the elevator scenes, as opposites, showing both in different sides, however, still connected to each other, is in some sort of way hiding the emotions that ena feels, and after they disconnect, in act 5 "therapy" the mask is agitated, exaggerating everything and being super active, even bouncing around the screen, meanwhile in the background, ena is just crying, having a meltdown or something.  and when she finally says how she can't 5:20 This is probably my favorite part of this episode, and i feel like a lot of Youtubers/content creators can relate to. Ena tries to get joy out of performing on stage (aka, performing for an audience, like a youtuber or content creator does) but although Ena can sense that the people watching the performance are enjoying it, Ena herself can't seem to find joy in it. It's even sadder a moment later when she calls it a "chore" meaning that she sees the performance more as work, rather than something that fulfills her, similar to how a Youtuber may feel trapped in a content hole of only being able to produce videos that perform well, rather than producing videos that they truly enjoy.

I may be completely wrong here, but this episode feels like it has a particular focus on art. ENA holds up her mask like Hamlet holds up the skull, and she explores several different forms of artistic expression. Though she can understand what the interest is on a technical level, and she can respect the performers as well as their audience, she can't understand why she's not feeling the joy that others are. It impacts her, but instead of bringing happiness, all she got were "incomprehensible feelings". The therapist's answer is that she cannot change herself in a way to find "fun" in this kind of art, sometimes something just doesn't fit with you. But then the ending comes in almost like a punchline: when Moony asks her if the place was any fun, ENA states that it was "stuffy", AKA "not receptive to new or unusual ideas; conventional and narrow-minded", and then a scene plays out more nonsensical than anything any of the other performers had in store. Her problem was not that she doesn't understand art, but that she got stuck inside the boxes of conventional artforms.  tl;dr art is niche, and with this weird webseries, every fan here has found their niche.

Hm, now correct me if i'm misremembering, but i feel as though this is following the aftermath of ENA's wish in Temptation Stairway. In said installment: she wished for eternal happiness, shown by her blue side turning yellow at the end. However, as shown here in Power of Potluck; the wish only gave her a mask to SEEM eternally happy, when in truth, she still feels the sadness she sported before she made her wish, now only without the ability to express it.  Since this isn't the first time she ventured to this place, it's clear that she has been attending this therapist for quite a while. Perhaps the more times she attended these sessions, the more she came to view this wish for "eternal happiness" as a parasite only making her miserable, inflicting her with a case of smiling depression. Her second yellow side returning to blue, now only with a manic mask obscuring her sorrow, seems to show her recognizing more and more that this "joy" is only artificial, and isn't helping her feel better.  I feel as though the mask combusting is a visual metaphor for ENA finally being able to mentally free herself of this "eternal happiness" and being able to express her sorrow once more. Despite her not feeling any better in the moment, it's clear she's already made tremendous progress, enough for her to be able to continue her path to healing without the aid of her therapist.  Honestly, i applaud this installment! It manages to continue the plot in a way that feels warranted, and not out of place, as well as giving another fascinating perspective to the end of Temptation Stairway. This might be my new favorite in the ENA series!

Just as ENA observed this "play," always on the verge of understanding on some level, yet never quite comprehending...so I observe this video.  And yet I enjoy it. So this is "fun"...I think.
So, one of the things about Ena is that she mostly talks with her happy side. Like, throughout all of the videos so far, the happy side gets the most lines, especially of lines that actually move conversations forward or serve to interact with others. The sad side gets comedic asides and bits that mostly go ignored, or are treated as annoying and rude by the other characters.  And that goes for this video as well - in fact, Ena doesn't use her sad side at any point up until the mask is destroyed. Given the mask is credited as a different character, and that it doesn't use the same dialect (the uwu speak) of her sad side, I'm going to count that as not her sad side speaking.  But the emotional climax of this one seems to be about Ena denying her sad side, masking it for the sake of others, and seeking happiness at the sad side's expense. And the biggest line in this video was the sad side's, acknowledging her true negative feelings rather than the performative thing she does normally.  Idk if that's going to end up meaning something for her sad side going forward (especially considering the game is eschewing happy/sad for a different pairing). But it have some interesting interplay with previous videos, at least.
